              Matrix of Reform Measures

                                          MALI

                RFFORM PROGRAM SUPPORTEDBY THE FIRST
              POVERTY REDUCTION SUPPORT CREDIT (PRSC 1)




1 OBJECTIVES OF THE REFORM PROGRAM

 1. The First Poverty Reduction Support Credit (PRSC-1) is part of the World Bank's
 support for implementing Mali's poverty reduction strategy. Its goals are to support the
 Government's efforts towards macroeconomic stabilization; to strengthen the foundations
 for strong, sustainable and equitable economic growth; and to improve access for
 underprivileged populations to basic social services. It continues earlier efforts aimed at:
 (i) strengthening and deepening reforms undertaken by the Government in recent years
 under two Structural Adjustment Credits (SAC IDand SAC IV)and the Economic Policy
 and Public Finance Management Credit; (ii) assisting the Government's implementation
 of the Growth and Poverty Reduction Strategy Framework (2007-2011 GPRSF), which is
 Mali's second generation poverty reduction strategy; and (iii) strengthening efforts by the
 authorities to create the conditions for increased assistance by Mali's technical and
 financial partners for the implementation of the GPRSF, by supporting selected reforms
 that enhance the integrity of the budget process and ultimately improve the efficiency of
 direct budget support.

 2. The Government has prepared a Growth and Poverty Reduction Strategy Framework
 (GPRSF) that describes the macroeconomic, structural and social policies and programs to
 promote growth and reduce poverty during 2007-2011. This new strategy takes into
 account the following key findings from the evaluation of implementation of the 2002-
 2006 PRSF: (i) maintaining a stable macroeconomic environment and better aligning
 macroeconomic and budget estimates as well as external funding contributions; (ii)
 improving consistency between the strategies, priorities and budget programming of the
 Medium Term Budget Framework (MTBF) and sectoral Medium Term Expenditure
 Framework (MTEF), in particular, action plans and detailed sectoral funding; (iii)
 significantly reducing poverty and hunger especially in the rural areas, based on an
 effective development of food security; (iv) improving the health status of the population
 especially the very poor; (v) significantly improving the quantity and quality of education
 services; (vi) creating a conducive environment for the development of the private sector
 and structural reforms such as privatizations (CMDT, SOTELMA), (vii) continuing and
 accelerating the State's reforms regarding decentralization, deconcentration and public
 finance.

 3. The 2007-2011 GPRSF has two major objectives: (i) promoting a robust annual
 growth rate of 7% by creating wealth and employment in growth-enhancing sectors such
 as rural production (agriculture, livestock, fishing, agro forestry, h i t s and vegetables),
 mining, energy and services (commerce, handicraft, tourism, culture, information
 technology and communications). Successhl growth of these promising sectors depends
 on presence of explicit energy strategies that integrate the various alternative energy

 sources. Effective management of population growth and better redistribution of wealth
 will reduce inequalities and unequal accessto basic social servicesthat are major causes of
 poverty; and (ii) improving public administration through the continuation, consolidation
 and deepening of reforms relating to the institutional framework (decentralization and
 deconcentration), political governance (democracy, fight against corruption and rule of
 law), economic governance (microfinance and the private sector) and social sector
 services (education,health, in particular, the fight against HIVIAIDS).

 4. The Poverty Reduction Support Credit will assist in accomplishing the objectives of
 the GPRSF, which is the first stage of a 10-year action plan to achieve the Millennium
 Development Goals. The PRSC's three components are aligned with the GPRSF's three
 strategic orientations, namely: (i) development of infrastructure and productive sectors,
 supported under the PRSC's second component; (ii) deepening of structural reforms,
 which is supported under the first and second PRSC components; and (iii) strengthening
 the social sector, supported under the third component of the credit.

 5. The first program component regards the strengthening of public finance
 management. It consists of two elements aimed at: (i) strengtheningthe macroeconomic
 framework and fiscal policies; and (ii) improvingpublic procurement.

 6. The second component regards promotion of economic growth to achieve the
 Government's poverty reduction objectives. The policy measures cover the financial
 sector, export promotion and the creation of a more conducive investment climate,
 transport and transit facilitation, electricity and drinking water, the cotton sector and the
  Office du Niger.

 7. The third component focuses on improving the access of vulnerable populations to
 basic social services, comprising the implementation of programs in: (i) health and social
 development, and (ii) rural water supply(outsidethe EDM water distribution system).


2 PROGRAM COMPONENTS

 8. The following actions were envisaged :(i) strengthening the overall consistencyof the
 budget with the poverty reduction strategy, and improving sectoral resources allocation
 mechanisms (the medium term budget framework); (ii) improving intra-sectoralresources
  allocation based on the sector development policies objectives (medium term Expenditure
  frameworks in the health, education and infrastructural sectors), and (iii) to strengthening
 the consistency between GPRSF and the budget law. These measures will deepen the
 actions supported by the two preceding operations, to enhance the overall visibility of
 public policies and the medium term budget policy so as to help pave the way for a
 gradual shift from project assistance toward budget support.

 9. In order to strengthen the organizational framework for integration of the PRSF
 process with the budget process, a logical framework was adopted to ensure greater
 consistency between the budget, the macroeconomic framework, sector priorities and the
 PRSF process.

2.1   Component 1: Strengthening public finance management

    10. In recent years a number of studies and evaluations have highlighted the strengths and
   weaknesses of Mali's budget system. Taking these analyses and recommended reforms
   into consideration, the Governmentprepared and adopted the Government Action Plan for
   Modernizing and Strengthening Public Finance Management (PAGAMGFP). The
   profound changes to be carried out under this program over the medium term (2006-2008)
   will enhance control over the budgetary process. The PAGAMGFP has five strategic
   pillars: (i) to improve the quality of preparation and implementation of the budget;(ii) to
    develop efficiency in fiscal and financial administrations; (iii) to incorporate external
    funds into national budget procedures; (iv) to increase efficiency and transparency in
    government procurement procedures (v); and to strengthen good governance and
   transparency.

    11. The reform program supported by the Poverty Reduction Support Credit is consistent
   with the PAGAMGFP and the 2007-2011 Growth and Poverty Reduction Strategy
    Framework. The objectives of the credit's public finance management component are: (i)
   to strengthen the links between the poverty reduction strategy and the sector strategies; (ii)
   to improve and modernize public finance management; and (iii) to strengthen the
   monitoring of budget execution. The reform measures are detailed in the attached policy
   matrix.


  2.1.1 Progress in recentyears and 2006

    12. The overall progress on budget management has been significant. In 2006, the
    Government pursued implementation of the PAGAMGFP, which is the framework of
   reference for donor support to Mali's public finance management. The PAGAMGFP will
   remain will continue to receive particular emphasis in the years ahead in the context of
    implementingthe second generation poverty reduction strategy (2007-2011 GPRSF). As a
   whole, progress has been satisfactorily achieved on the three objectives set out in PRSC-1.
   The 2006 actions were all achieved and the program prospects for 2007 and 2008 are
    favorable.


      2.1.1.1 The Fiscal and Budget Policy in the MacroeconomicFramework

    13. For some years now, the Government has pursued prudent macroeconomic
   management policies. It has emphasized macroeconomic stabilization while maintaining
   the level of resources allocated to social sectors notwithstanding the economy's
   vulnerability to climatic shocks and fluctuations in the international product prices (raw
   materials, especially petroleum products). This rigorous macroeconomic management will
   continue in the 2007-2011 period. The 2007 budget adopted by the National Assembly
   emphasizesthese principles. Its policy orientations are in line with economic prospects for
   2007.


      2.1.1.2 Budget Management

   14. Based on the proposed institutional mechanism for implementation of the
   PAGAMGFP, the Government has taken specific actions whose impact is critical to the

success of the entire reform process. These actions include: (i) establishment of
coordination and management entities (e.g., technical committee, and Public Finance
Reform Support Unit (CARFIP)whose coordinator was nominated); (ii) adopting a logical
framework for implementation and follow-up of the PAGAMGFP; and (iii) implementing
the 2006 actions of the PAGAMGFP. In addition, the Government, assisted by the donor
community, evaluated the institutional framework to establish a benchmark for its public
finance performance based on the Public Expenditure and Financial Accountability
(PEFA)methodology. The benchmark rating was approved in early2007.

15. In the area of budget preparation, the Government designed and introduced various
instruments in the budget process to ensure coordination between public policies and the
budget. This results-based budget management process introduced in 1998 was further
strengthened, resulting in significant improvements in the medium-term expenditure
frameworkprocess of the budget formulationprocess:

 - The Government prepared a medium-term budget framework (MTBF) for the 2007-
    2011 period to facilitateimplementation of the 2007-2011 PRSP. The MTBF is based
    on recent macroeconomic developments in Mali, medium-term prospects envisaged in
    the GPRSF, the economic environment facing the West African Economic and
    Monetary Union (WAEMU), and constraints due to the international economic
    environment. The Government prepared budget resource estimates for the 2007-2011
    period (its own resources and external resources). It also established preliminary
    expenditure allocation estimates, taking into account Mali's macroeconomic
    constraints on the one hand, and on the other, priorities for the social sectors and
    production support sectors.

 - At the sector level, the MTEF for education, health and social development, State
    reform, decentralization, equipment and transportation, and territorial administration
    sectors are all operational and regularly updated. The MTEF for the Ministry of
    Employment and Professional Training is in the process of being approved. The
    MTEFs for the rural sector, water supply and sanitation, industry and commerce,
    promotion of women, children and the family, and handicraft and tourism, are all
    currentlybeing prepared.

 - Based on the ten-year health and social development program (PRODESS) and the
    ten-year education development program (PRODEC), an institutional framework was
    adopted that creates a synergy between the Ministry of Finance and the various
    sectoral ministries to support their actions in proposing their respectiveMTEF.

16. As regards budget execution, the actions taken focused mainly largely been on
computerizing budget information flows, and building on the improvements made in
standardizing procedures and disseminatingthem among all budget-process actors. These
actions were initiated under the preceding credit and are ongoing within the PRSC
framework. Thus, in 2006, there were improvements in the information system of the
Budget Department and budget administrators in sector ministries (financial
administration departments-DAFs).        The "improved" version of the budget software
(PRED 4) was extended to the Financial Control Department and the Treasury and Public
Accounting Department. In line with the agreed timetable, the Government commenced

 the process to connect four (4) DAFs and four (4) regional budget departments (DRB)
 based on the computerized budget system developed by the Information Technology and
 Communications Agency (AGETIC).

  17. As regards budget control, the Government remains convinced of the need to
 strengthen control functions in any feasible way (administratively, internally, externally,
 jurisdictionally and legislatively). The improvements made were as follows: (i) resources
 provided to the Finance Inspection and General Control of Public Services Departments
 were in line with the results expected fiom these departments under the 2006 budget, in
 terms of oversight and the quality of control reports; (ii) the Accounts Section of the
  Supreme Court (Section des comptes) obtained the resources required for its 2006 work
 program; (iii) the legislative texts required to increase the Accounts Section staff from 15
 to 67 magistrates were revised, and discussions are underway toward formulating the
 mandates of the magistrates.

  18. As regards transparency and budget execution monitoring mechanisms, two
  aspects were significantly improved, toward systematic and timely production of budget
 information. These were: (i) the publication of economic and financial information on the
 website of the Ministry of Economy and Finance. It provides essential data to the general
 public on State budget execution; and (ii) the improvement of the quarterly public finance
 report. To strengthen its accountabilityin management of public resource, the Governrnent
 cleared the backlog in preparation of the draft budget execution reports and
 producedladopted the draft 2005 budget execution report. Further strengthening will be
 achieved under the credit through effortsto reduce the time taken to produce the report.


    2.1.1.3 Government Procurement

  19. The World Bank reviewed Mali's procurement procedures (CPAR) and formulated a
 number of proposals to strengthen the regulatory and institutional framework for
 Government procurement and improve the procedures. This report (CPAR) was adopted
 by the Council of Ministers in early 2007. The committee charged with the coordination
 and monitoringthe Governmentprocurement reform process (CNCS) was established and
 is functional. The Governrnent also established a database covering the various
 procurement stages.


2.1.2 Medium-termActions

 20. Through its public finance management component, the reform program to be
 supported by the second and third PRSCs, will have the same objectives as that of the
 PFM component of the PRSC-1, as described in paragraph 11. Specific actions supported
 by the PRSC are described in the policy matrix annexed to the current LDP.

      Strengthenlinks between poverty reduction and sector strategies

 21. Over the next two years, the Government will continue to strengthen actions already
 undertaken in budget preparation and its link with the poverty reduction strategy. This will
 entail an expansion of the MTEF process and operationalizingthe logical framework to
 enable better communication between sector departments and the MEF on CSCRP

   implementation. Actions to be implemented include: (i) expanding the MTEF process to
   food security and the environment, and annual updating of all existing MTEFs (health,
   education, agriculture, livestock and fisheries, water and sanitation) for 2008-2010 by
   September 2007; and (ii) expandingthe MTEF process to at least two more sectorswhile
   continuing to update by end-September 2008 existingMTEFs for the period 2009-201 1.

       Strengthen and modernize public finance management

   22. The GOM will fully opaationalize the institutionalmechanisms for implementation of
   the PAGAMGFP, inclusive of monitoring and evaluation (M&E) mechanisms. These will
   take effect with the joint reviews by the GOM and its technical and financial partners to
   evaluate program implementation for the respective year. The annual time table will be
   formally adopted by PAGAMGFPYsTechnical Committee each January, and implemented
   and evaluated in the course of the year by the Committee institutional framework. The
   performance measurement framework for public finance management will be applied
   every three years to measure progress compared to the baseline. The resulting actions for
   the PRSC policy matrix include: (i) preparing, adopting (in January 2007), and
   implementing the updated 2007 program of the PFM Action Plan (PAGAMGFP) (2007);
   and (ii) preparing, adopting (in January 2008), and implementing the updated 2008
   PAGAMGFP(2008) program.

       Strengthenthe budget monitoring system

   23. The GOM will continue its computerization efforts, including the building of a
   computerized network linking key actors of the public expenditure system. Specifically,it
   will: (i) operationalize the network connection with four sector ministry DAF units and
   four DRBs, based on the AGETIC infrastructure; (ii) begin network extension to the
   regions in September 2007; and (iii) finalize the operational network with all DAFs and
   regions in September2008.

       Strengthenthe procurement system

   24. Actions to strengthen procurement will include: (i) adoption by the Council of
   Ministers of the draft Decree on the Procurement Code; (ii) adoption by the GOM of the
   draft texts for creating the procurement regulatory department, and the department to audit
   procurement transactions; (iii) strengthening of the capacities and responsibilities of the
   contracting authorities; (iv) installation of a database with an integrated procurement
   management system in four ministries; (v) installation of the two bodies (regulatory and
   auditing); and (vi) use of the indicators and performance standards (Baseline Indicators
   System)highlighted in the CPAR.


2.2  Component2: Support to growth

   25. The GOM already introduced policy actions, supported under the previous operation
   based on the results of analytical studies previously undertaken. These reforms comprise
   sectors contributing to economic growth, notably financial sector development, transport
   and transit facilitation, export promotion and investment climate, electricity and water
   supply, cotton, and refonns in the OfficeduNiger irrigation zone.

2.2.1 Financial sector

  26. During the last two years, the GOM implemented actions that complement efforts to
  strengthen the role of the financial sector in economic growth. It also worked to create a
 business environment that encourages banks to mobilize long-term resources and offer
  financialservicesand medium- and long-term credit at lower cost.


    2.2.1.1 Actions taken in 2006

  27. The GOM pursued and deepened the actions undertaken in the previous operation. In
  this context:

      the Government undertook discussions on the repayment mechanism for non-
      performing loans proposed in the final 2006 audit report commissionedby the GOM.
      Implementing the proposed mechanism proved difficult and reformulation is needed.
      The revised mechanism would entail individual negotiations with banks to define an
      appropriate strategy for each one. For this purpose, the authorities (i) invited
      commercial banks to implement the recommendations of the consultant report
      regarding improvement of lending procedures and credit monitoring, (ii) intervened to
      facilitate recovery of non-performing loans, and (iii) held meetings with commercial
      banks to reach consensus on portfolio clean-up strategies.

   - the Board of Directors of Banque de I'Habitat du Mali (Malian Housing Bank; BHM)
      appointed a new chief executive officer, and an inter-bank loan was negotiated to
      strengthenthe bank's capital. A monitoring committee including GOM representatives
      and sector professionals was also established to strengthen bank management and
      operations, and bank authorities implemented restructuring measures to strengthen
      institutional solvency, liquidity, and efficiency to enable the bank to accommodate
      withdrawals and restart lending activities.

   - the Supreme Court reached a decision in favor of the Government regarding ownership
      of the shares of the Banque Internationale pour le Mali (International Bank for Mali;
      BIM); the sale of BIM shares owned by the Government could proceed, within the
      context of BIM7srestructuring; various restructuring measures were also implemented
      to strengthenBIM solvency and efficiency.

   - the Government established a committee to monitor implementation of the
      recommendations of the study on domiciliation of insurance policies. Measures were
      taken to implement regulations on compulsoryautomobile insurance.

   - as regards microfinance, the action plan for the period 2005-2008 was adopted and
      implemented. Supervision and promotion activities were separated, with supervision
      activities now handled by the CCSISFD unit in the Ministry of Economy and Finance,
      and promotion activities by the CPAISFD unit in the Ministry for Promotion of
      Investments and Small and Medium-sized Enterprises. Under the 2007 budget,
      resources were allocated to cover a part of the operating costs of the CCSISFD and
      CPAISFD units.

  - the review of the pension code of the Caisse de Retraite du Mali (Mali Pension Fund;
     CRM), was finalized in August 2004. In addition, following the actuarial study, the
     Council of Ministers approved (on June 21,2006) a parametric reform package for the
     civil service pension system to graduallyreducing the financial deficit of the CRM in
     the medium term. This reduction will be made through adjustments to various
     parameters such as the rate of contribution, retirement age, and the benefit levels.
     Negotiations with stakeholders are in process, prior to submission to the National
     Assembly of the CRM bill authorizing the parametric reforms.

  - in March 2006, an actuarial study of the Institut National de Prkvoyance Sociale
     (National Institute of Social Welfare; INPS) for non-civil servant employees of the
     public and private sectors, was completed. Implementation of the plan negotiated and
     signedwith the GOM for cleaning up bad debts, was also initiated.


    2.2.1.2 Medium-termreforms

 28. Policy actions during 2007-2009 will include: (i) continuing negotiations with
 commercial banks to formulate strategies for each bank aimed at strengthening
 mechanisms for analysis, approval, monitoring, and recovery of loans, and mechanisms
 for cleaning-up non-performing loans in the bank portfolios; (ii) strengtheningmandatory
 insurance controls; (iii) continuing the BHM reorganization plan; (iv) implementing the
 BIM restructuring plan, including its privatization; (v) revision of the texts pertaining to
 the INPS, and their adoption by the GOM in April 2007; and (vii) submitting to the
 National. Assembly in April 2007 the new CRM law authorizing the parameter reforms,
 and adopting the decree for its implementation.


2.2.2 Private sector development

 29. Actions taken by the GOM within the framework of the PRSC aim to contributeto an
 enhanced investment climate and export development. Specific activities include the
 facilitation of company start-ups, implementation of the recommendations of the
 integrated trade diagnostics study, elimination of the expertise tax for export of artisan
 products, and adoption of quality standards for export industries, including agricultural
 products.


    2.2.2.1 Actions taken in 2006

 30. In order to reduce the complexity, time, and cost of creating a business, the GOM
 adopted a law enabling the collapsing of five procedures (involving five different
 administrations) into one. For this purpose, in July 2006 the National Assembly adopted a
 law creatingthe singleID number for firms.This law was enacted on August 11,2006.

 31. To encourage exports, an inter-ministerial decree was signed in October 2006 by the
 ministries for artisan industries and culture to eliminate (i) the expertisetax for exports of
 artisan products and (ii) the need for export authorization for these products from the
 National Museum. This action will be implemented mainly through a public awareness
 campaign targeting artisans. The GOM also developed criteria for distinguishing

 antiquities from artisan products (appraisal services will be provided by the National
 Museum, which will charge a service fee).


    2.2.2.2 Medium-termreforms

 32. The following policy actions will be taken: (i) formulation and adoption of quality
 standards for export industries, particularly agriculturalproducts; (ii) establishment of the
 one-stop window for investors based on the new operational texts for one-stop window
 taking into account the single ID law; (iii) waiving of the license requirement for the first
 calendar year for all new businesses; (vi) reduction of the required procedures, time, and
 cost of creating a company; (v) in the context of a new general tax code, reduction of
 property registration fees for buildings acquired by firms for business purposes; and
 implementation of measures to further reduce taxes; (vi) conducting a study of corporate
 taxation in Mali on investment, capital gains, savings, and salary income, and
 implementation of the recommendations of the study during 2008; (vii) undertaking a
  study on labor market competitiveness and initiation of discussionson implementation of
 the recommendations in 2008; (vii) supporting the development of export-oriented sectors
 through information sharing, training, and supplychain improvements; and (viii) adoption
 of the texts on regulation and management of the industrialzones.


2.2.3 Transport and transit facilitation


    2.2.3.1 Actions taken in 2006

 33. Efforts were focused on road maintenance. In the 2006 finance law, the GOM raised
 the level of resources allocated for road maintenance to 11.5 billion CFAF in line with the
 commitmentsit made within the framework of the transport sector program. However, the
 share of road-use fee revenues of the Road Authority, which should be 30% of the road
 maintenance budget, would be only about 16% (1.7 billion CFAF instead of 3.5 billion).
 To ensure effective road maintenance for 2006, the GOM financed the gap of 1.8 billion
 CFAF f?om the interdepartmentalcommon funds during execution of the 2006 budget.

 34. To improve the predictability of the Road Authority's resources and to gradually
 achieve the agreed goal in preceding LDPs of a 40% share of revenue from road users, the
 GOM added a separate line for the road-use fee in the petrol import price structure.

 35. To improve the competitiveness and quality of road transporters, terms of reference
 were elaborated for (i) a study of taxes and special levies on (road) transport operators,
 and (ii) a studyon creating a competitive freight exchange.

 36. To improve the round-trip time of freight vehicles, the followingmeasures were taken
 to reduce customs processing times: (i) reducing the number of customs declarations
 subject to the "red" risk circuit category through the use of risk analysis; (ii) unloading
 into customs bonded warehouses the freight of all vehicles not cleared by the owners
 within 72 hours; (iii) allowing the collection of customs duties on Friday afternoons,
 Saturdays, and Sundays; and (iv) eliminating customs escorts for road freight authorized
 under the Interstate Road TransitFacilitation system.

 37. A diagnostic audit of the General Customs Department was undertaken in 2006 by the
 World Customs Organization (WCO).

 38. In order to improve governance on transport corridors, a decision was taken to put
 emphasis on (i) implementing regulations pertaining to road checkpoints and barriers
 inside Mali and ensuring control-free passage for traffic authorized under the Interstate
 Road Transit Facilitation system (TransitRoutier hter-~trrt,TRIE); and (ii) preparing
 instructions, budgets, and public awareness campaigns for government workers and users.


    2.2.3.2 Medium-term reforms

 39. In 2007, the GOM will implement policy measures to increasethe revenue shareof the
 Road Authorityto the stated goal of 40% of the 2008road maintenance budget.

 40. To improvethe competitiveness and quality of transport, the GOM will: (i) adopt draft
 bills on various tax measures and special levies, together with an implementation
 timetable; and (ii) study and define a pilot freight exchange mechanism to be put into
  operation in 2007.

  41. To reduce the customsprocessing time for vehicles, the recommendations of the 2006
  external audit undertaken by the WCO will be implemented, and an internal audit will be
  undertaken. The audit will cover current customs clearance time and waiting times for
 trucks processed at the FaladiC and railwaycustoms centers.

  42. To improve governance of transport corridors and accelerate transit and round-trip
  times across Mali's access corridors, the mandate and means available to the national
  facilitation committee will be strengthened, as well as monitoring of public awareness
 programs targeting various authorities. The Transit Observatory (OT) will collect
  statistics,and the MEF and Ministry of Equipment and Transport (MET) will commission
  an adual audit of the results.


2.2.4   Electricity and urban water supply

  43. New strategies and policies will address major challenges in the energy sectorwith the
  goal of providing accessible services in all areas to as many people and production
  facilitiesas possible at the lowest cost. These challengesinclude:

   - finding an alternative to firewood to protect forest resources and stop illegal logging
      practices;

   - introducingbetter management at EDM (Mali Electricity and Water utility company);

   - identimng the financing needed to carry out priority projects and programs for the
      next five years.

  44. The GOM intervention strategy is defined in the Letter of Sector Policy for Electricity
  and Water Supply adopted on November 10, 1999. This policy defines measures
  regarding:

  - strengtheningof the institutionaland legal frameworkof the energy sector;

  - development of domestic energy and rural electrification;

  - promotion of alternative energyusing traditional fuels;

  - development of a national securitystockpile of hydrocarbons;

  - developmentof a national computerized network;

  - development of renewable energy; and

  - promotion of research on hydrocarbons and fuels (solid and gaseous).

 45. With respect to the electricity sector, GOM core goals include: (i) cleaning up EDM's
  financial situation; (ii) ensuring adequate energy services; (iii) establishing institutional
  arrangements for sustainable management; (iv) establishing objectives, principles, and
 rational pricing mechanisms; (v) installing efficient regulation tools; (vi) continuing and
  enhancing activities for the development of rural electrification and domestic energy; (vii)
  establishing sub-regional grids, (viii) developing biofuels and nonrenewable energy
  (ENR); and (ix)buildingpublic-private partnerships.


    2.2.4.1 Actions in 2006

  46. Based on the strategic management plan for EDM approved in January 2006, the
  GOM: (i) launched a management audit, (ii) commissioned a tariff study, (iii)
  commissioned an institutional study, (iv) developed optimal investment plans for
  electricity, and (v) commenced measures to ensure the financial viability of the company.
  These actions took longer than expected, but will be finalized in the medium term.


    2.2.4.2 Medium-termactions

  47. Medium-term actions will include the followingpolicy measures: (i) validation of the
  conclusions of the studies identified under EDM's strategic management plan
  (management audit, institutional study, optimal investment plans, EDM technical and
  financial audit for 2000, 2004 et 2005), (iii) implementation of the recommendations of
 the management audit, (iv) implementation of the recommendations of the institutional
  study, (v) establishment of the new managerial entities for electricity and water supply,
  (vi) adoption of the optimal investment plans for electricity, (viii) approval of the
  simulationmodel, and (ix) application of the tariff regulation principles.


                                     1
2.2.5 The cotton sector

 48. Implementing and strengthening the cotton sector reform process are priorities for the
 GOM as this will enhance the sector's driving force in economic growth and the income
 securityof rural populations. The GOM is aware of the need to continue these reforms and
 attain full privatization of the CMDT so as to minimize the sector's risk to the
 Government budget and hence to poverty reduction programs. The Government confirms
 its firm commitmentto the process.

 49. The cotton producer price-setting mechanism adopted by the GOM in January 2005
 continuesto be implemented so as to minimize the potential risks of this commodityto the
 national budget.

 50. With agreement from its principal stakeholders, the GOM defined four zones for
 privatization and the Council of Ministers adopted the final operational scheme for the
 privatization.

 51. Implementation of the detailed processing timetable is progressing as planned and as
 such is a strong indication of the Government's commitment to move forward with the
 privatization process. Prior to splitting up the sector for sale, a review of the accounting
 and financial situation of the CMDT will be undertaken. The terms of reference for the
 evaluation are already available. The recruited consultant's responsibility will comprise:
 (i) a complete review of CMDT's accounts for 2004, 2005 and 2006, and provision of an
 opinion on the company's financial situation; (ii) examine CMDT's accounts for the 2004-
 05, 2005-06 and 2006-07 crop seasons with a view to understanding the main difference
 between them; (iii) analyze CMDT's cash position through a review of the extent of debt
 liquidity and enforceability of claims on the company, and verify the cash flow forecasts
 for 2007 and 2008; (vi) analyze CMDT's medium and long term indebtedness,and assess
 the measures proposed to pay off those debts; and (v) review in detail the internal control
 mechanisms. The evaluation is expected to be completed in July 2007.

 52. Given that the definition of the zones and adoption of the operational scheme
  constitute two key stages of this process, the GOM will make provisions to facilitate
 completion of the cotton sector reforms so as to achieve total privatization of the CMDT
 in 2008. The final stages will include the continued implementation of the revised time
  line for cotton sectorreform adoptedby the Council of Ministers on December28,2005.


2.2.6 Niger Office irrigation (ON)

  53. Generally, actions supported by the PRSC aim to: (i) install a reliable private sector
 mechanism for irrigation financing in the ON, and (ii) adopt an improved system for
 management of the ON and for evaluating its performance.


    2.2.6.1 Program undertaken in 2006

  54. Actions implemented in 2006 are the continuation of those began by the GOM under
 the preceding operation and also under the National Rural Infrastructure Program
  supported by the World Bank. In this context:

   - the Government completed an initial allocated of plots to the private sector in the
     experimental Koumouna perimeter; taking into account comments received from
     technical and financial partners, a thorough analysis of the results was undertaken. The
     new call for a tender was issued and the opening of the bids took place on January 14,
     2007.

   - the Cellule de gestionfoncigre (Land Management Unit) was placed under the ON'S
     DirectorateGeneral to strengthenits performance.

    -  a complementary study was initiated to strengthen the financing aspects of the private
       sector irrigation financing mechanism to increase the ON area developed through
       private funding.

    -  in order to improve the ON'S performance management within a framework for
       development of the zone, an organizational audit was completed.


     2.2.6.2 Next phase of the reforms

   55. Actions will include: (i) adoption by the Council of Ministers of the draft texts for the
   creation of the ON department charged with managing irrigation financing; (ii) adoption
   by the GOM of the master plan for the ON zone; (iii) adoption by the ON Board of
   Directors of the action plan of the ON organizational audit; (iv) establishment of the
   department charged with managing irrigation financing and transfer of land titles; and (v)
   implementation of the ON organizational audit action plan adopted by the ON Board.


2.3  Component3: Access to basic social services

   56. Access to basic social services is a priority of the Growth and Poverty Reduction
   Strategic Framework. It includes two programs: health and social development, and water
   supplyoutside the EDM zone.


 2.3.1 Actions planned for 2006

   57. As part of implementing the health and social development program, several actions
   were implemented in 2006 to improve the supply and quality of health services. They
   include: (i) finalizing and implementing the standard performance contract with the
   hospitals; (ii) defining a plan to strengthen family planning services offered by the
   community health centers (CSCOMs) and the health referral centers (CSREFs); (iii)
   confirming the provisions taken to cover the financing gap of the 2007 operational plans
   of the ministries of health and social development; and (iv) increasing the share of current
   resources transferred to sub-national central government units.


 2.3.2 Medium-termactions

   58. Under the health and social development program, the following actions will be
   implemented:

   59. To improve the supply and quality of health services, actions will include (i)
   implementing the performance contracts with the hospitals; (ii) adoption of annual budgets
   for health and social development ministries based on the ministries' respective MTEFs
   including, for 2008, a provisional health map taking the private sector into account in the
   statistics on existing centers; (iii) gradually increasing the share of current resources
   transfen-ed to sub-national central government units; and (iv) increasing the number of
   operational CSCOMs.

 60, To increase the use of public and private health services, actions will include: (i)
 finalization of standard contracts for NGOs and private sector entities (MDS); and (ii)
 extension of coverage by communityhealth insuranceprograms (mutuelles).

 61. With regard to the drinking water program (outside the EDM zone), the
 Government's priority is to implement the National Water Supply Program (NWSP)
 aimed at achievingthe Millennium Development Goals (MDG) for the sector (i.e., provide
 75% of the population with access to a water supply by 2015). The NWSP will be
 translated into action within a framework of integration with the updated sanitation
 strategy. The program objectives are to: (i) provide all villages with at least one potable
 water supply tap (currently lacking in 2,000 villages); (ii) implement the cost recovery
 policy to ensure sustainable water supply taps (currently 30% of the 25,000 taps are
 nonfunctional); (iii) provide support to the communities to allow them to plan, operate,
 and manage the infrastructure; (iv) promote the delegation of management of the water
 delivery systems to local private operators; and finally (v) successfully integrate the
 promotion of good sanitation and hygiene practices with water supply programs to
 increase the impact on public health.

 62. The following actions will be undertaken in 2007 to improve access to sustainableand
 affordable drinking water: (i) review and updating of the national water department's
 mandate, taking into account the planning and monitoring mission of the water sector
 program; et (ii) finalization of the new strategy for maintenance of the potable water taps,
 which aims to improve the sustainabilityof the infrastructure,program the rehabilitation
 of the 8,000 nonfunctional potable water taps, and promote the delegation of the
 management of piped water systemsthrough public-private partnerships.


3 MONITORING THE REFORM PROGRAM

 63. To strengthen monitoring of the policy matrix, coordination will be assured by the
 Secretary General of the Ministry of Economy and Finance (MEF) in liaison with the
 respective ministries. To ensure better monitoring by all ministries concerned, all
 measures pertaining to the prior actions for the PRSC-2 will be integrated in the
 Government's work program (Program de Travail Gouvernemental). Implementation of
 these measures will be monitored monthly and reported on in meeting minutes. Other
 policy actions will be monitored quarterly by the MEF, together with the other ministries
 involved.

                   ANNEX 4: DONOR HARMONIZATION PROCESS




1. Since the 2003 Donor Round Table held in Geneva to mobilize resources for
implementation of Mali's poverty reduction strategy(PRSF 2002-2006), the Governmenthas
expressed its willingnessto establish a framework for public policy management conducive to
a transition toward increased budget support. This is part of Mali's agenda for implementing
the Paris Declaration on Harmonizationand Alignment.


DONORORGANIZATIONIN MALI(CONSULTATION MECHANISMS)

2. The following consultation mechanisms exist in Mali for Government-donor and intra-
donor dialogue:

           The Mixed Mali-Donor Commission meets quarterly comprising Government and
           donor representatives.It is co-chaired by the Minister of Economy and Finance and
           the lead donor agency (designated for a six-month term rotating alternatively
           between bilateral and multilateral agencies);

           Intra-donor consultation occurs monthly. The meeting, which is chaired by the lead
           donor agency supported by the preceding and subsequent lead donor agency,
           discusses current developments in Mali and specific themes relating to PRSF
           implementation;

           Donor thematic groups, which meet more regularly as needed, provide feedback to
           the monthly meetings. Each thematic group meeting is chaired by a designated lead
           donor and comprises donors involved or interested in the group's theme. The
           thematic groups comprise technical staff but occasionally include donor agency
           heads for information sharingand decision making purposes.


BUDGET    SUPPORTAS AN INSTRUMENT OF HARMONIZATION

3. In principle, all donors involved in the donor consultations subscribe to the Paris
Declaration, and seek ways with the Mali Government to operationalize it. A thematic
working group on harmonization that has been in place since 2004, focusing with the
Government on defining the mechanisms for implementing common budget support
fi-arneworkby Mali's donors. Furtherwork is needed to reach the harmonizationobjectives.

4. Current progress toward harmonization comprises the signing of the following between
the Government and donors:

           A Framework Arrangement for budget support (MOU) expressing the commitment
           of the signatoriesto adopt a common set of general principles for budget support to
           Mali; six donors including the World Bank signed the MOU with the Government
           in March 2006;

          Specific Arrangements for budget support to the education and health sectors (The
          Netherlands) as well as to support the decentralization process (European
          Commission); the World Bank is not a signatoryto the specificarrangements.

5. Sector budget support (i.e., the specific arrangements for health, education and
decentralization) enables: (i) donors to establish a programmatic approach in the main priority
sectors using national procedures for public finance management and procurement; and (ii)
enhanced donor coordination on program design and conditionalityas well as the institutional
framework for monitoringand evaluation of program implementation.

6. Currently, a specific arrangement for general budget support (i.e., not earmarked to a
sector) is being finalized, together with donors providing budget support or balance of
payment support. The PRSC falls into this categoryof arrangements.


fie WorldBank's role

7. The World Bank is the lead donor in Mali on public finance management and budget
support. The Bank led the technical discussions that culminated in the signature of the
Framework Arrangement for budget support to Mali. The Bank is currentlyworking with the
Malian authorities and other donors to finalize the specific arrangement for general budget
support,and is overseeing the donor support PEFA exercise.


General architecture of budget support to Mali

          A framework arrangementthat outlines the general principles for budget support to
          Mali

          Specific arrangements aimed at clarifying: (i) the practical modalities for
          implementing the framework arrangement for general budget support, consistent
          with Mali's budget cycle and minimizing the transactions costs in terms of design,
          monitoring and evaluation (predictablity, joint evaluations, coordinated policy
          matrices); (i) common mechanisms for provision of sector-specificbudget support
          consistent with Mali's budget cycle and national implementationprocedures .


Principlesfor general budget support

8. Discussions on the general principles for implementing budget support are ongoing
between the donors and the Government.The followingpartial agreements havebeen reached:

       Announcement(predictability of budget support). Joint annual announcements of
       donor support over the medium term would be made by end April at the latest, to
       enable updating of the medium term budget framework. The announcements would be
       confirmed in September/October to provide advance information for the subsequent
       year's budget preparation process.

       Disbursements would be made preferably during the first or third quarters of the
       calendar year.

       Monitoring and coordination would be made through a committee comprising
      representatives of the Ministry of Economy et Finance (chair), Ministry of Planning
       and Land Management, PRSF Unit and donors signatory to the Arrangement; the
       committee would meet twice a year (in JuneIJuly and November) and on an ad hoc
      basis as needed:

           1. The June/July meeting would review progress in implementing the
               conditionalities to enable donors with disbursements programmed for the third
               quarter of the year to assess whether to disburse; update the list of
               conditionalities for the subsequent year to enable the second disbursement that
               is based on the review of PRSF indicators and structural and sectoral reform
               programs; updating of the list of conditionalities for the subsequent year, to
               clarifL key actions (exclusive of progress on PRSF indicators) required for
               release of the first quarter disbursement;

           2. TheNovember meeting would review the conditionalities (based on outcome of
               joint missions and the 2"d IMF mission) to assess whether to release the next
               year's 1stquarter disbursement.

       Missions would preferably be joint so as to minimize the transaction costs for the
       Government, and preferably scheduled in line with Mali's budget calendar and PRSF
       reviews.


TeE PRSCAND THE GOVERNMENT'S             AGENDA FOR ALIGNEMENT ET HARMONISATION

9. The PRSC is expected to be consistent with the general principles above as well as with
national priorities, given that the Bank's is a signatory to the general budget support
Arrangement with the other concerned donors (Sweden, France, The Netherlands, Canada,
African Development Bank, and European Commission). It should also be made consistent in
time with the final arrangement that emerges from the ongoing discussions.

10.In line with the principles above, the PRSC process could be structured according to the
proposed schematic,which takes into account Mali's budget cycle, the PRSF process, and the
Government's preference for disbursements to be made in either the first or third quarters of
each year. The schematicincludestiming of missions and disbursements for PRSC's 1,2 et 3.

                           ANNEX 6: FUND RELATIONS NOTE

                        Mali-Assessment Letterfor the World Bank

                                        January 30,2007


Further to the completionof the fourth review under the PRGF arrangement on a lapse of time
basis in July 2006,16this note provides a preliminary assessment of Mali's macroeconomic
conditionsand outlook as well as an update on relationswith the IMF.'~

Mali's reform and stabilization efforts since 1996 have been supported by the Fund
through financial and technical assistance. This includes support under two three-year
Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility (PRGF) arrangementsduring 1999-2003and the
current three-year PRGF arrangement, which was approved by the Executive Board in June
2004. Mali reached the completionpoint under the enhanced HIPC Initiative in March 2003
and received SDR75 million in debt relief under the MDRI from the Fund in early January
2006. In November 2006, a mission concluded ad referendum discussions on the fifth review
under the current PRGF arrangement, with a possibleBoard meeting in February 2007.

Mali's recent performance under the PRGF program has been uneven. The authorities
have met all quantitativeperformance criteria for the fifth review but missed most of the
structural benchmarks. Prudent fiscal policybacked by developmentpartner support, includ-
ing MDRI, has secured reasonablegrowth, low inflation, and a sustainable external debt
position. In contrast, lackluster structuralrefoms have left the country highly vulnerableto
exogenous shocks.

        The authorities kept their fiscal program on track through the end of September
        by taking new measures.A shortfall in revenue (0.8 percent of GDP at the end of
        September)prompted the authoritiesto curtail non-povertyrelated spendingplans
        (0.6 percent of GDP) and, startingin September, to implement additionalrevenue
       measures.As a result, the authoritiesmet all the PRGF's program's quantitative
       performancecriteria for the end of September2006. However,the poor revenue
       performance meant that the indicativetargets for tax revenue and the basic balance
       were not met.

       Mali's external environmentwas favorablein 2006. Terms of trade strengthened,as
       higher gold prices more than offset the rise in internationaloil prices. Thanks to
       MDFU, externaldebt sustainabilityremained well within the threshold levels and is
        expectedto strengthen further.




16See Mali--FourthReview Under the Three-YearArrangementUnder the PovertyReduction and
GrowthFacility and Request for Waiver of Nonobservance of Performance Criterion,EBS/06/83,
June 30,2006.

" Based on information availablethrough November 2006.

rn     Owing to an improved external environment, the economy is maintaining
       momentum and inflation is falling. Real GDP growth is projected to grow by 5 per-
       cent in 2006, as a result of a good 2005106 cereal harvest, higher gold production, and
       emerging growth in services. Tracking developments in food prices, the inflation rate
       is projected to decrease to less than 2 percent in 2006. Mali's favorableinflation
       differential with its trading partners has partly offset the nominal appreciation of the
       CFA franc against the U.S. dollar.

       However, progressin structural reforms has been slow since the fourth PRGP
       review was completedin July. In particular, there are continued delays in (i) intro-
       ducing a petroleumpricing mechanism linkedto world prices; (ii) presenting civil
       servicepension (CRM) reform legislation to the National Assembly; (iii) attracting
       private sector interest in the recapitalization of the Banque de I 'Habitatdu Mali
       (BHM); (iv) progressing with privatization of the Banque Internationale du Mali
       (BIM);and (v) proceedingwith the studiesnecessaryto preparethe stateenergy
       companyEnergie du Mali (EdM) for reprivatization. The Council of Ministers (i)
       approvedin June a package of parametric reforms that would--once the decree is
       issued-gradually    reduce the projected deficit of the civil servicepension; and (ii)
       adopted in October an operationalplan for the privatization of the state-owned cotton
       ginning company (CMDT) in 2008.

The authorities have expressedtheir renewed commitmentto the objectives of the
PRGP, which expires in June 2007. The 2007 fiscal framework is reasonablyprudent and
should not require recourse to domestic financing. Its implementationshould be facilitated by
the authorities' decisionto allow for a full pass through of internationaloil prices into
domestic prices. Another key commitmentthat would impact public financesin the years to
come is the decisionto submit to parliament legislation to reform the CRM. Furthermore, the
authoritiesrecognizethat strengtheningthe financial system and reinforcing governance of
state-ownedenterprisesare the immediate stepsneeded to realize Mali's growth potential.

       In the banking sector, priority will be given to strengthening the balance sheets of
       a number of public institutionsand increasing the role of the private sector. The
       authorities are committed to fully support the restructuringplan of BHM, in
       consultation with the World Bank, but will not issue any new loans or guarantees in its
       favor. Privatization in the banking sector should continue in 2007-08 and a
       comprehensive financial sector development strategyshouldbe launched.

       At CMDT and EdM, the priorityis to address governance problems to improve
       productivityand safeguardpublic finances.The authoritieswill strengthen their
       surveillanceof CMDT's and EdM's cash flow operationsto limit their operating
       lossesin 2007. The staff emphasizedthe importanceof ensuringthat these companies
       remains commerciallyviable in preparation for their planned privatization in 2008.

Beyond the period covered by the current PRGF, the authorities are committed to
improving Mali's difficult business climate. The second-generation PRSP (2007-11)

appropriatelyplaces private-sector-led growth as the cornerstone of the development strategy.
If forcehlly and consistentlyimplemented in an action plan that refocuses the state in its core
functions, Mali could confidentlycontemplatea higher pace of economic growth than the
current 5percent trend rate and achieve a significant reduction in poverty.

Main policy risks center around effective implementation of key structural reforms to
improve governance and avoid an energy andlor cotton crisis. Failure to implement much
needed structural reforms would discourage investmentand possiblydonor support,generate
socialpressures, and undermine Mali's medium-term economic and social objectives.Policy-
making in the immediate future will be furthercomplicated by the political calendar, as well
as by the continued volatile situationin the northernpart of Mali and in neighboring C8te
d71voire.Mali will also remain vulnerable to exogenousdevelopments,notablypotential
drought and terms of trade shocks.

                            ANNEX 7:PROGRESS ON THE MDGs

       Progress to date for various indicators suggest that Mali may not reach some of the
MDG targets. There are eight MDGs in the declaration adopted by the United Nations. The first
seven MDGs can be grouped into four categories: a) eradicating extreme poverty; b) eradicating
hunger; c) Achieving universal primary education and promoting gender equality; and d) improving
health outcomes and ensuring environmental sustainability. The eighth MDG relates to the
development of a global partnership for development. Data on the progress achieved so far for the
indicators related to these goals are given in Table A7.1. A more detailed discussion (together with
explanationson the data sources used for the estimation) is availableas well as in the November 2004
report entitled Rapport de suivi de la mise en oeuvre des Objectifs du Millknaire pour le
Dkveloppement (OMD) and prepared with the support of UNDP.

       Eradicating extremepoverty (Goal I). The first MDG includes two objectives, the first one of
       which is the eradication of extreme poverty understood as the inability for households to
       generate enough resources in order to meet their basic needs. To monitor progress, the target
       is to reduce extreme poverty by half between 1990 and 2015, and the main indicator is the
        share of the population living below a Purchasing Power Parity poverty line of US$1 per day.
       In practice, rather than using the US$l poverty line, it is better to rely on a country-specific
       methodology for the estimation of poverty in order to track progress towards that goal.
       Estimates prepared by DNSI suggest relatively slow progress towards reducing poverty, with
       the share of the population in poverty declining from 72-73 percent in 1989to 68.3percent in
       2001. Alternative estimates based on the cost of basic needs method suggest faster progress,
       with the poverty headcount reduced from 63.8 percent in 1989 to 56.5 percent in 2001. In
        fact, the reduction has been larger since the 1994 devaluation, and this is confirmed using
       data on assets owned by household in repeated demographic and health surveys. But even
       then, achieving a reductionby half of poverty by 2015 will require higher growth rates in the
        future as comparedto the (already relatively good) performance observed in the 1990s.

       Eradicating hunger (Goal I). The second objective in the first MDG is the eradication of
       hunger, with as target a reduction by half the share of the population which suffers from
       hunger. The indicators for this target are the prevalence of child malnutrition, as well as
        estimates of the share of the population without adequate dietary energy consumption.Data
        on child malnutrition are available from the nationally representative Demographic and
        Health Surveys. Child malnutrition as measured by stunting actually increased between 1991
        and 2001, from 27.1 percent to 38.0 percent, but other indicators such as wasting showed an
        improvement, from 42.9 percent to 33.0 percent. Overall, despiteprogress in some indicators,
        it remains unclear whether a reduction in the various indicators of malnutritionand hunger by
        half in 2015 versus 1990levels is likely.

       Achieving universal primary education and promoting gender equality (Goals 2 and 3). The
       next two MDGs are to achieve universal primary education and promote gender equality. The
        target for universal primary education is the completion of a full course of primary schooling
       by boys and girls alike. There are three indicators to measure progress: the net enrollment
       ratio in primary education, the proportion of pupils starting grade 1 who reach grade 5, and
        the illiteracy rate of 15-24year-olds. The target for gender equality and the empowerment of
        women is the elimination of gender disparities in primary and secondaryeducation by 2005,
        and for all levels of education by 2015. The four indicators suggested for monitoringprogress
        over time are the ratio of girls to boys in primary, secondary and tertiary education, the ratio
        of literate females to males of 15-24 year-olds, the ratio of women to men in wage
        employment in the non-agricultural sector, and the proportion of seats held by women in

national parliament. The data in Table A7.1 suggests significant progress. For example, the
gross enrollment rate in primary school increased fiom 26.0 percent in 1990to 67.0 percent in
2003, and the ratio of girls to boys in primary schools increased from 0.62 to 0.73 over the
same period. As for the literacy rate among the population aged 14 to 25, it has increased
fiom 18.8percent in 1991 to 41.5 percent in 2001. A continuation of this trend might enable
Mali to reach the MDGs.

Improving health outcomes and ensuring environmental sustainability (Goals 4 to 7). The
fourth and fifth MDGs are essentially to reduce child and maternal mortality. The targets for
child mortality are to reduce by two thirds, between 1990 and 2015, the under-five mortality
rate (with three indicators: the under-five mortality rate, the infant mortality rate, and the
proportion of one year old children immunized against measles). The targets for maternal
mortality are to reduce by three quarters, between 1990and 2015, the maternal mortality ratio
(with two indicators: the maternal mortality ratio itself and the proportion of births attended
by slulled health personnel). Unfortunately, as shown in Table A7.1, progress is fairly limited
in the indicators for infant, child, and maternal mortality. Today, only a minority of women
benefit from a medically assisted delivery. The sixth MDG is also related to health: it consists
in combating and reversing the spread of HIV/AIDS, malaria, and other communicable
diseases. There, some progress is achieved, in so far as Mali has been able to avoid high rates
of HIVIAIDS infection. The seventh MDG is to ensure environmental sustainability. While
there are many indicators here, an important one consists in halving by 2015 the proportion of
people without sustainable access to safe drinking water. Strong progress has been achieved
here, with the share of the population with such access increasing from 38.0 percent to 54.1
percent.

Building a global partnership for development: Selected indicators related to this goal are
also provided in Table A7.1. After the adoption of its PRSF, Mali became in March 2003 the
7' countryto achieve the completion point for debtrelief under the HIF'C initiative, which has
enabled the country to reduce key debt ratios, including the debt service to export ratio which
has been reduced by more than half. In line with the priorities established in Mali's PRSF,
resources from debt relief are being allocated to priority social sectors and poverty reduction
activities. More generally, during the period 1993-2002, about 60 percent of development
assistancewas allocated to basic social services.
